        <th colspan="2" style="background-color: lavender; text-align: center">Global</th> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <th><i><a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">ARWU</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Rankings_ARWU_W_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rankings_ARWU_W-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></th> 
        <td>101-150</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <th><i><a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></th> 
        <td>126</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <th><i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Rankings_THES_W_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rankings_THES_W-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></th> 
        <td>135</td> 
       </tr> 
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <p>In 2009 and 2010, <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> ranked the University of Virginia as the number two public university among &quot;National Universities&quot; in the United States and <sup><span style="font-variant:small-caps">#</span></sup>130 among the world's best universities.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> In the 2011 edition, the undergraduate program at U.Va. ranked <sup><span style="font-variant:small-caps">#</span></sup>2 out of roughly 200 public universities in the United States, tied with <a href="/wiki/UCLA" title="UCLA" class="mw-redirect">UCLA</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-usnews-public2011_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usnews-public2011-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> and <sup><span style="font-variant:small-caps">#</span></sup>25 overall (including private schools), tied with <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Los_Angeles" title="University of California, Los Angeles">UCLA</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_California" title="University of Southern California">University of Southern California</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wake_Forest_University" title="Wake Forest University">Wake Forest University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> In the 26-year history of the rankings, U.Va. has never dropped out of the Top 25 listing and has always ranked either <sup><span style="font-variant:small-caps">#</span></sup>1 or <sup><span style="font-variant:small-caps">#</span></sup>2 among public schools.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> In every published edition of the report going back to 1983, the undergraduate program at the University has also retained its position as the highest ranked school, public or private, in its home state of Virginia. <a href="/wiki/Forbes_Magazine" title="Forbes Magazine" class="mw-redirect">Forbes Magazine</a> ranked the University <sup><span style="font-variant:small-caps">#</span></sup>44 in its 2010 ranking of U.S. universities, the highest ranking for a public university on the list.<sup id="cite_ref-forbes2010_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes2010-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> Internationally, in 2010 U.Va. ranked 72nd in the world according to the <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-World_University_Rankings_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_University_Rankings-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> The 2011 <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a> placed Virginia at 126th overall, four places up from 2011, and 96th in Arts &amp; Humanities.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> GQ magazine recognized the University of Virginia noting classroom attendance of scholarship athletes as well as student traditions such as referring to the institution as &quot;the University,&quot; ranking it 25th.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The University of Virginia has been recognized numerous times as having the highest <a href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">African American</a> graduation rate among public universities, and by a wide margin.<sup id="cite_ref-virginia.edu_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-virginia.edu-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-jbhe.com_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jbhe.com-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> Among the Top Four public universities that consistently rank highest in the <i>U.S. News</i> rankings, the University of Virginia has an 87% black student graduation rate, some 15 to 20 percentage points higher than the 70% at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Berkeley" title="University of California, Berkeley">University of California, Berkeley</a>, 68% at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Michigan" title="University of Michigan">University of Michigan</a>, and 73% at <a href="/wiki/UCLA" title="UCLA" class="mw-redirect">UCLA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-jbhe.com_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jbhe.com-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, due in part to <a href="/wiki/California_Proposition_209_(1996)" title="California Proposition 209 (1996)">California Proposition 209</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Civil_Rights_Initiative" title="Michigan Civil Rights Initiative">Michigan Proposal 2</a>, the University also has much higher African American populations than these peer universities. The University of Virginia has an undergraduate student body that is 8.7%<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> African American, while the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California" title="University of California">University of California</a> undergraduate student bodies at Berkeley and UCLA are just 3.2%<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> and 3.7%<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> African American, respectively. Only 5.2%<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> of University of Michigan undergraduates are African American. Thus, relative to its closest peers, the University of Virginia has twice to three times the proportion of African American undergraduate students, and they go on to graduate at significantly higher rates.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="(February 2013)">why?</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <p>The University of Virginia has many highly regarded graduate programs. Programs ranked in their respective fields' top 10 by <i>U.S. News &amp; World Report</i> include <a href="/wiki/Law" title="Law">Law</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tax_Law" title="Tax Law" class="mw-redirect">Tax Law</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Law" title="International Law" class="mw-redirect">International Law</a>, <a href="/wiki/Architecture" title="Architecture">architecture</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> 18th through 20th Century <a href="/wiki/British_Literature" title="British Literature" class="mw-redirect">British Literature</a>, <a href="/wiki/African-American_Literature" title="African-American Literature" class="mw-redirect">African-American Literature</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_Literature" title="American Literature" class="mw-redirect">American Literature</a>, American Literature Before 1865, <a href="/wiki/Creative_Writing" title="Creative Writing" class="mw-redirect">Creative Writing</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Colonial_history_of_the_United_States" title="Colonial history of the United States">U.S. Colonial History</a>, <a href="/wiki/Political_Theory" title="Political Theory" class="mw-redirect">Political Theory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Developmental_Psychology" title="Developmental Psychology" class="mw-redirect">Developmental Psychology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Medical-surgical_nursing" title="Medical-surgical nursing">Adult/Medical-Surgical Nursing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Psychiatric_and_mental_health_nursing" title="Psychiatric and mental health nursing">Psychiatric/Mental Health Nursing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Management" title="Management">Management</a>, <a href="/wiki/Primary_education" title="Primary education">Elementary Teacher Education</a>, <a href="/wiki/Secondary_education" title="Secondary education">Secondary Teacher Education</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Special_Education" title="Special Education" class="mw-redirect">Special Education</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Edgar_Allan_Poe_crop.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Edgar_Allan_Poe_crop.jpg/175px-Edgar_Allan_Poe_crop.jpg" width="175" height="216" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Edgar_Allan_Poe_crop.jpg/263px-Edgar_Allan_Poe_crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Edgar_Allan_Poe_crop.jpg/350px-Edgar_Allan_Poe_crop.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Edgar_Allan_Poe_crop.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Allan_Poe" title="Edgar Allan Poe">Edgar Allan Poe</a> attended the University during its second session in 1826, taking classes in French and German while columns were still being constructed on the original Rotunda.
        <sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Scholars_Foundation" title="Jefferson Scholars Foundation">Jefferson Scholars Foundation</a> offers four-year full-tuition scholarships based on regional, international, and at-large competitions. Students are nominated by their high schools, interviewed, then invited to weekend-long series of tests of character, aptitude, and general suitability. Approximately 3% of those nominated successfully earn the scholarship.</p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/University_of_Virginia_College_of_Arts_%26_Sciences#Echols_Scholars" title="University of Virginia College of Arts &amp; Sciences" class="mw-redirect">Echols Scholars</a> (College of Arts and Sciences) and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Virginia_School_of_Engineering_and_Applied_Science#Rodman_Scholars_Program" title="University of Virginia School of Engineering and Applied Science">Rodman Scholars</a> (School of Engineering and Applied Sciences), which include 6-7% of undergraduate students, receive no financial benefits, but are entitled to special advisors, priority course registration, residence in designated dorms and fewer curricular constraints than other students.<sup id="cite_ref-echols-benefits_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-echols-benefits-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The University offers 48 <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor's degree">bachelor's degrees</a>, 94 <a href="/wiki/Master%27s_degree" title="Master's degree">master's degrees</a>, 55 <a href="/wiki/Doctorate" title="Doctorate">doctoral degrees</a>, 6 educational specialist degrees, and 2 first-professional degrees (<a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Medicine" title="Doctor of Medicine">Medicine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Juris_Doctor" title="Juris Doctor">Law</a>) to its students.</p> 
     <p>The University of Virginia Library System holds 5 million volumes. Its Electronic Text Center, established in 1992, has put 70,000 books online as well as 350,000 images that go with them. These e-texts are open to anyone and, as of 2002<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=University_of_Virginia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, were receiving 37,000 daily visits (compared to 6,000 daily visitors to the physical libraries).<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The University of Virginia is a member of a consortium engaged in the construction and operation of the <a href="/wiki/Large_Binocular_Telescope" title="Large Binocular Telescope">Large Binocular Telescope</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Mount_Graham_International_Observatory" title="Mount Graham International Observatory">Mount Graham International Observatory</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Pinaleno_Mountains" title="Pinaleno Mountains">Pinaleno Mountains</a> of southeastern <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a>. It is also a member of both the Astrophysical Research Consortium, which operates telescopes at <a href="/wiki/Apache_Point_Observatory" title="Apache Point Observatory">Apache Point Observatory</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Universities_for_Research_in_Astronomy" title="Association of Universities for Research in Astronomy">Association of Universities for Research in Astronomy</a> which operates the <a href="/wiki/National_Optical_Astronomy_Observatory" title="National Optical Astronomy Observatory">National Optical Astronomy Observatory</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Gemini_Observatory" title="Gemini Observatory">Gemini Observatory</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Space_Telescope_Science_Institute" title="Space Telescope Science Institute">Space Telescope Science Institute</a>. The University of Virginia hosts the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/National_Radio_Astronomy_Observatory" title="National Radio Astronomy Observatory">National Radio Astronomy Observatory</a>, which operates the <a href="/wiki/Green_Bank_Telescope" title="Green Bank Telescope">Green Bank Telescope</a> in <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia" title="West Virginia">West Virginia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Very_Large_Array" title="Very Large Array">Very Large Array</a> radio telescope made famous in the <a href="/wiki/Carl_Sagan" title="Carl Sagan">Carl Sagan</a> television documentary <i><a href="/wiki/Cosmos:_A_Personal_Voyage" title="Cosmos: A Personal Voyage">Cosmos</a></i> and film <i><a href="/wiki/Contact_(film)" title="Contact (film)">Contact</a></i>. The North American <a href="/wiki/Atacama_Large_Millimeter_Array" title="Atacama Large Millimeter Array">Atacama Large Millimeter Array</a> Science Center is also located at the Charlottesville NRAO site.</p> 
     <p>UVA also hosts the <a href="/wiki/Rare_Book_School" title="Rare Book School">Rare Book School</a>, a non-profit organization that studies the history of books and printing. The University is one of 60 elected members of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a>, and the only member representing the Commonwealth of Virginia. Along with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Connecticut" title="University of Connecticut">University of Connecticut</a>, UVA is one of two American member universities of <a href="/wiki/Universitas_21" title="Universitas 21">Universitas 21</a>, an international consortium of research-intensive universities. On May 14, 2007, then-University President John Casteen was named Chairman of the Board of the organization.</p> 
     <p>The university campus was recognized by MSN as one of the most beautiful college campuses in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Undergraduate_placement_into_graduate_school_programs">Undergraduate placement into graduate school programs</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Undergraduate placement into graduate school programs">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In 2003, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i> studied the undergraduate backgrounds of entering students at &quot;elite&quot; graduate programs.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> The University of Virginia with 82 placements (2.6% of class) placed 33rd overall and third among all state-supported universities in elite graduate placement.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> No other state university on the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="East Coast of the United States">Atlantic Seaboard</a> had greater than one-third the number of placements as the University of Virginia.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculty">Faculty</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Faculty">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:KathrynThornton.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/KathrynThornton.jpg/175px-KathrynThornton.jpg" width="175" height="221" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/KathrynThornton.jpg/263px-KathrynThornton.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/KathrynThornton.jpg/350px-KathrynThornton.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:KathrynThornton.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Kathryn_C._Thornton" title="Kathryn C. Thornton">Kathryn C. Thornton</a>, Associate Dean for Graduate Programs at the 
        <a href="/wiki/University_of_Virginia_School_of_Engineering_and_Applied_Science" title="University of Virginia School of Engineering and Applied Science">School of Engineering and Applied Science</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Virginia possesses a distinguished faculty, including a Nobel Laureate, a <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> winner and former U.S. poet laureate, 25 Guggenheim fellows, 26 Fulbright fellows, six National Endowment for the Humanities fellows, two Presidential Young Investigator Award winners, three Sloan award winners, three Packard Foundation Award winners, and a winner of the 2005 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physiology_or_Medicine" title="Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine">Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> The University's faculty were particularly instrumental in the evolution of Internet networking and connectivity. Physics professor James McCarthy was the lead academic liaison to the government in the establishment of <a href="/wiki/Suranet" title="Suranet" class="mw-redirect">SURANET</a>, and the University has also participated in <a href="/wiki/Arpanet" title="Arpanet" class="mw-redirect">ARPANET</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abilene_Network" title="Abilene Network">Abilene</a>, <a href="/wiki/Internet2" title="Internet2">Internet2</a>, and <a href="/wiki/National_LambdaRail" title="National LambdaRail">Lambda Rail</a>. On March 19, 1986 the University's <a href="/wiki/Domain_name" title="Domain name">domain name</a>, <tt>Virginia.edu</tt>, became the first registration under the <tt><a href="/wiki/.edu" title=".edu">.edu</a></tt> <a href="/wiki/Top-level_domain" title="Top-level domain">top-level domain</a> originating from the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_(U.S._state)" title="Commonwealth (U.S. state)">Commonwealth</a> of <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Faculty were originally housed in the <a href="/wiki/The_Lawn" title="The Lawn">Academical Village</a> among the students, serving as both instructors and advisors, continuing on to include the McCormick Road Old Dorms, though this has been phased out in favor of undergraduate student resident advisors (RAs). Several of the faculty, however, continue the University tradition of living on Grounds, either on the Lawn in the various Pavilions, or as fellows at one of three residential colleges (<a href="/wiki/Brown_College_at_Monroe_Hill" title="Brown College at Monroe Hill">Brown College at Monroe Hill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hereford_College" title="Hereford College">Hereford College</a>, and the International Residential College).</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Poet_Rita_Dove_receives_the_2011_National_Medal_of_Arts_from_President_Barack_Obama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/82/Poet_Rita_Dove_receives_the_2011_National_Medal_of_Arts_from_President_Barack_Obama.jpg/220px-Poet_Rita_Dove_receives_the_2011_National_Medal_of_Arts_from_President_Barack_Obama.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/82/Poet_Rita_Dove_receives_the_2011_National_Medal_of_Arts_from_President_Barack_Obama.jpg/330px-Poet_Rita_Dove_receives_the_2011_National_Medal_of_Arts_from_President_Barack_Obama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/82/Poet_Rita_Dove_receives_the_2011_National_Medal_of_Arts_from_President_Barack_Obama.jpg/440px-Poet_Rita_Dove_receives_the_2011_National_Medal_of_Arts_from_President_Barack_Obama.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Poet_Rita_Dove_receives_the_2011_National_Medal_of_Arts_from_President_Barack_Obama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Commonwealth professor of English and former U.S. poet laureate Rita Dove receives the 2011 National Medal of Arts from President Barack Obama.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Some of the University of Virginia's faculty have become well-known national personalities during their time in <a href="/wiki/Charlottesville" title="Charlottesville" class="mw-redirect">Charlottesville</a>. <a href="/wiki/Larry_Sabato" title="Larry Sabato">Larry Sabato</a> has, according to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i>, become the most cited professor in the country by national and regional news organizations, both on the Internet and in print.<sup id="cite_ref-Sabato_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sabato-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> Civil Rights activist <a href="/wiki/Julian_Bond" title="Julian Bond">Julian Bond</a>, a professor in the Corcoran Department of History from 1990 until his retirement in 2012, was the Chairman of the <a href="/wiki/NAACP" title="NAACP" class="mw-redirect">NAACP</a> from 1998 to 2009. Professor Bond was also chosen to be the moderator of the 1998 Nobel Laureates Conferences, which included His Holiness the Dalai Lama, Archbishop Desmond Tutu, and other living winners of the Nobel Peace Prize. <a href="/wiki/Media_Studies" title="Media Studies" class="mw-redirect">Media Studies</a> and Law professor <a href="/wiki/Siva_Vaidhyanathan" title="Siva Vaidhyanathan">Siva Vaidhyanathan</a>, an expert in <a href="/wiki/Copyright_law" title="Copyright law" class="mw-redirect">copyright law</a> and Internet issues, moved from <a href="/wiki/New_York_University" title="New York University">New York University</a> to the University of Virginia in 2007. Spanish professor David Gies received the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Isabella_the_Catholic" title="Order of Isabella the Catholic">Order of Isabella the Catholic</a> from King <a href="/wiki/Juan_Carlos_I_of_Spain" title="Juan Carlos I of Spain">Juan Carlos I of Spain</a> in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> 1987 <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize_for_poetry" title="Pulitzer Prize for poetry" class="mw-redirect">Pulitzer Prize for poetry</a> recipient <a href="/wiki/Rita_Dove" title="Rita Dove">Rita Dove</a>, professor in the English department since 1989, served as <a href="/wiki/United_States_Poet_Laureate" title="United States Poet Laureate">United States Poet Laureate</a> from 1993 to 1995; in 1995, together with former U.S. president <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Carter" title="Jimmy Carter">Jimmy Carter</a>, she chaired an unprecedented gathering of Nobel laureates in literature in Atlanta. In 1996 Rita Dove received the <a href="/wiki/National_Humanities_Medal" title="National Humanities Medal">National Humanities Medal</a> from President <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>, and President Barack Obama honored her with the 2011 <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Arts" title="National Medal of Arts">National Medal of Arts</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> making her only the fourth person, after novelists <a href="/wiki/Eudora_Welty" title="Eudora Welty">Eudora Welty</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Updike" title="John Updike">John Updike</a> and <a href="/wiki/Philip_Roth" title="Philip Roth">Philip Roth</a>, and the only poet to receive both of the highest United States honors for lifetime achievement in the arts and humanities.</p> 
     <p>In 2002, the <i><a href="/wiki/Cavalier_Daily" title="Cavalier Daily" class="mw-redirect">Cavalier Daily</a></i> student newspaper began annually posting faculty compensation online.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

     <p>The University is also endowed with several affiliated centers including the <a href="/wiki/Rare_Book_School" title="Rare Book School">Rare Book School</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Center_for_Chemistry_of_the_Universe&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Center for Chemistry of the Universe (page does not exist)">Center for Chemistry of the Universe</a>, headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/National_Radio_Astronomy_Observatory" title="National Radio Astronomy Observatory">National Radio Astronomy Observatory</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Virginia_Center_for_Politics" title="University of Virginia Center for Politics">University of Virginia Center for Politics</a>, Weldon Cooper Center for Public Service, <a href="/wiki/Sorensen_Institute_for_Political_Leadership" title="Sorensen Institute for Political Leadership">Sorensen Institute for Political Leadership</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Miller_Center_of_Public_Affairs" title="Miller Center of Public Affairs">Miller Center of Public Affairs</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Fralin_Museum_of_Art" title="Fralin Museum of Art">Fralin Museum of Art</a> is dedicated to creating an environment where both the University community and the general public can study and learn from directly experiencing works of art.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_strength">Financial strength</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Financial strength">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Endowment_and_Fundraising">Endowment and Fundraising</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Endowment and Fundraising">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Managed by the University of Virginia Investment Management Company, and with <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">$</a>4.8 <a href="/wiki/1000000000_(number)" title="1000000000 (number)" class="mw-redirect">billion</a> as of February 2013, U Va's endowment ranked 19th among all colleges and universities, and fifth among public universities.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2006, then-President Casteen announced an ambitious $3 billion capital campaign to be completed by December 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> U Va missed the 2011 deadline, and extended it indefinitely.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> At the graduation ceremonies in May 2013 President Sullivan announced that U Va. had met its goal of raising $3 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Triple-A_credit_rating">Triple-A credit rating</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Triple-A credit rating">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The University of Virginia is one of only two public universities in the U.S. that has a <a href="/wiki/Bond_credit_rating" title="Bond credit rating">Triple-A credit rating</a> from all three major credit rating agencies, along with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Texas_at_Austin" title="University of Texas at Austin">University of Texas at Austin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> This allows it to borrow money and fund projects with the best possible conditions and terms.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Cavaliers" title="Virginia Cavaliers">Virginia Cavaliers</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Chris_Long_Gator_Bowl_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Chris_Long_Gator_Bowl_2008.jpg/175px-Chris_Long_Gator_Bowl_2008.jpg" width="175" height="263" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Chris_Long_Gator_Bowl_2008.jpg/263px-Chris_Long_Gator_Bowl_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Chris_Long_Gator_Bowl_2008.jpg/350px-Chris_Long_Gator_Bowl_2008.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Chris_Long_Gator_Bowl_2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Chris_Long_(American_football)" title="Chris Long (American football)" class="mw-redirect">Chris Long</a>, #2 overall pick of the 
        <a href="/wiki/2008_NFL_Draft" title="2008 NFL Draft">2008 NFL Draft</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Virginia's athletics program competes in <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a> (and the <a href="/wiki/Football_Bowl_Subdivision" title="Football Bowl Subdivision" class="mw-redirect">Football Bowl Subdivision</a> for <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a>), and has been a member of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coast_Conference" title="Atlantic Coast Conference">Atlantic Coast Conference</a> since 1953. The current Athletic Director at Virginia is <a href="/wiki/Craig_Littlepage" title="Craig Littlepage">Craig Littlepage</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Cavaliers" title="Virginia Cavaliers">Virginia Cavaliers</a>, also called &quot;Wahoos&quot; or &quot;Hoos&quot;, have won 21 recognized national championships, 16 of them since 1980. Virginia has won multiple national titles in seven different sports, including four men's sports (<a href="/wiki/Lacrosse" title="Lacrosse">lacrosse</a>, 7; <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">soccer</a>, 6; <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a>, 2; and <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a>, 1) and three women's sports (<a href="/wiki/Women%27s_lacrosse" title="Women's lacrosse">lacrosse</a>, 3; <a href="/wiki/Rowing_(sport)" title="Rowing (sport)">rowing</a>, 2; and <a href="/wiki/Cross_country_running" title="Cross country running">cross country</a>, 2). It also holds a national championship in <a href="/wiki/Track_and_field" title="Track and field">track and field</a>. The men's <a href="/wiki/College_basketball" title="College basketball">college basketball</a> team has won either the ACC regular season (1981, 1982, 1983, 1995, 2007) or <a href="/wiki/ACC_Tournament" title="ACC Tournament" class="mw-redirect">ACC Tournament</a> (1976) titles six times and has been to the <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship">Final Four</a> twice, while the women's squad has been three times.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Cavaliers_football" title="Virginia Cavaliers football">football team</a> won a share of the ACC Championship in both 1989 and 1995 (both before the conference had a championship game). After never reaching a bowl before 1984, the team has played in 17 bowl games since. The program is also notable for its recent high draft picks in the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/2006_NFL_Draft#Round_one" title="2006 NFL Draft">#4 overall pick</a> of 2006, <a href="/wiki/D%27Brickashaw_Ferguson" title="D'Brickashaw Ferguson">D'Brickashaw Ferguson</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/2008_NFL_Draft#First_round" title="2008 NFL Draft">#2 overall pick</a> of 2008, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Long_(American_football)" title="Chris Long (American football)" class="mw-redirect">Chris Long</a>. The program is a party to three major rivalry games in the conference: the longest series in the ACC, the <a href="/wiki/South%27s_Oldest_Rivalry" title="South's Oldest Rivalry">South's Oldest Rivalry</a> with <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Tar_Heels" title="North Carolina Tar Heels">North Carolina</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Cup" title="Commonwealth Cup" class="mw-redirect">Commonwealth Cup</a> with <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Tech_Hokies" title="Virginia Tech Hokies">Virginia Tech</a> (part of the greater <a href="/wiki/Virginia-Virginia_Tech_rivalry" title="Virginia-Virginia Tech rivalry" class="mw-redirect">Virginia-Virginia Tech rivalry</a>); and the <a href="/wiki/Maryland-Virginia_rivalry" title="Maryland-Virginia rivalry" class="mw-redirect">Beltway Brawl</a> with <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Terrapins" title="Maryland Terrapins">Maryland</a>. While the Cavaliers have played UNC more times (114) than any other rival, all of these opponents ? North Carolina, Virginia Tech, and Maryland ? each list Virginia as their schools' longest-standing football rivals.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <p>In 2006, the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Cavaliers_men%27s_lacrosse" title="Virginia Cavaliers men's lacrosse">men's lacrosse team</a> won its fourth <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Lacrosse_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Lacrosse Championship">NCAA Men's Lacrosse Championship</a>, and sixth including the pre-tournament era. In the title game, Virginia defeated <a href="/wiki/UMass_Minutemen" title="UMass Minutemen">UMass</a> 15-7 in front of a record crowd of 47,062 at <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Financial_Field" title="Lincoln Financial Field">Lincoln Financial Field</a> in <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>, the first lacrosse crowd to surpass the crowd size of the men's basketball Final Four and the largest crowd to witness any <a href="/wiki/Category:NCAA_championships" title="Category:NCAA championships">NCAA Championship</a> during the year.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> The team finished the season a perfect 17?0, the best record in NCAA lacrosse history. Five years later the Cavaliers won the 2011 championship behind eventual <a href="/wiki/Tewaaraton_Trophy" title="Tewaaraton Trophy">Tewaaraton Trophy</a> winner Steele Stanwick, bringing their tournament era championship total to 5, which puts them fourth amongst NCAA Division I teams and first amongst ACC Teams.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:ClaudioReyna_USMNT_20060511.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/ClaudioReyna_USMNT_20060511.jpg/175px-ClaudioReyna_USMNT_20060511.jpg" width="175" height="263" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/ClaudioReyna_USMNT_20060511.jpg/263px-ClaudioReyna_USMNT_20060511.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/ClaudioReyna_USMNT_20060511.jpg/350px-ClaudioReyna_USMNT_20060511.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:ClaudioReyna_USMNT_20060511.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Claudio_Reyna" title="Claudio Reyna">Claudio Reyna</a> won 3 national championships at Virginia and was later captain of the 
        <a href="/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_soccer_team" title="United States men's national soccer team">USA team</a> for the 
        <a href="/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2002 FIFA World Cup">2002</a> and 
        <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006</a> 
        <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">World Cups</a>. Dubbed &quot;
        <a href="/wiki/Captain_America" title="Captain America">Captain America</a>&quot; by his British fans, he was named 
        <a href="/wiki/Soccer_America_College_Team_of_the_Century#Player_of_the_Century" title="Soccer America College Team of the Century">Player of the Century</a> by 
        <i><a href="/wiki/Soccer_America" title="Soccer America">Soccer America</a></i>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The new <a href="/wiki/John_Paul_Jones_Arena" title="John Paul Jones Arena">John Paul Jones Arena</a> opened in the fall of 2006 for <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Cavaliers_men%27s_basketball" title="Virginia Cavaliers men's basketball">men's</a> and women's basketball. It seats 14,593 fans, making it the third largest on-campus basketball facility in the ACC and the largest arena not located in a <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_metropolitan_areas" title="List of United States metropolitan areas" class="mw-redirect">major metropolitan area</a>. The arena's inaugural year witnessed the Virginia men's basketball team's first place finish in the ACC.</p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Davenport_Field" title="Davenport Field">Davenport Field</a>, where the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Cavaliers_baseball" title="Virginia Cavaliers baseball">UVa baseball team</a> plays, is also new, opening in 2002. In <a href="/wiki/Brian_O%27Connor_(baseball_coach)" title="Brian O'Connor (baseball coach)">Brian O'Connor</a>'s first 4 seasons at the helm after being made the head baseball coach in July 2003, the team has averaged 44 wins per year and become a nationally ranked power. The team has led the ACC in team <a href="/wiki/Earned_run_average" title="Earned run average">ERA</a> for 4 consecutive years. In 2009, the baseball team won a place in the <a href="/wiki/College_World_Series" title="College World Series">College World Series</a> for the first time.</p> 
     <p>The soccer teams are also national powers, with men's soccer having won 6 national championships to date including its most recent in December 2009. The women's team is regularly ranked in the top 10 nationally. The teams play their home matches at <a href="/wiki/Kl%C3%B6ckner_Stadium" title="Kl&ouml;ckner Stadium">Kl&ouml;ckner Stadium</a>, the largest soccer stadium in the ACC. The men's team has been invited to the NCAA Tournament for 26 consecutive years and made the College Cup many times. Former Coach <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Arena" title="Bruce Arena">Bruce Arena</a> has coached the US national team and currently coaches the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Galaxy" title="Los Angeles Galaxy">Los Angeles Galaxy</a> in <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">Major League Soccer</a>.</p> 
     <p>The Aquatics and Fitness Center (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.virginia.edu/rcam/afc.html">webcam</a>) has been popular among University students for working out and swimming since its opening in Fall 1996, and it is also where the <a href="/wiki/Swimming_(sport)" title="Swimming (sport)">Swimming</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Diving" title="Diving">Diving</a> teams compete in home meets. The men's swimming and diving team won 8 consecutive ACC Championships between 1999 and 2006. The women's swimming team won its fourth consecutive ACC Championship on February 19, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Also winning consecutive ACC titles has been the men's tennis team, which has won 4 consecutive regular season ACC Championships. Playing their home matches at the <a href="/wiki/Sheridan_Snyder_Tennis_Center" title="Sheridan Snyder Tennis Center">Sheridan Snyder Tennis Center</a>, the men's tennis team had their best season ever in 2007, finishing with a 30-4 record and a #2 national ranking. <a href="/wiki/Somdev_Devvarman" title="Somdev Devvarman">Somdev Devvarman</a> became the first ACC player in conference history to win the NCAA Singles Championship, which he won in two consecutive years. In addition, the tennis team beat Ohio State for the 2008 National Indoor Tennis Championships, 4-1.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <p>Now that <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Tech_Hokies" title="Virginia Tech Hokies">Virginia Tech</a> has joined the ACC, the <a href="/wiki/Virginia-Virginia_Tech_rivalry" title="Virginia-Virginia Tech rivalry" class="mw-redirect">Virginia-Virginia Tech rivalry</a> has been strengthened across a number of sports. This rivalry between the University and its larger neighbor to the southwest is followed statewide.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> UVA's athletic teams have bested the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Tech_Hokies" title="Virginia Tech Hokies">Hokies</a> through the years in <a href="/wiki/Virginia-Virginia_Tech_rivalry#All-time_and_ACC_series_results" title="Virginia-Virginia Tech rivalry" class="mw-redirect">many of the major sports</a>. The two universities also faced off in the <a href="/wiki/Virginia-Virginia_Tech_rivalry#Commonwealth_Challenge" title="Virginia-Virginia Tech rivalry" class="mw-redirect">Commonwealth Challenge</a> between 2005 and 2007, with the Cavaliers routing the Hokies in each Challenge: 14.5 to 7.5 in 2005-2006 and 14 to 8 in 2006-2007. The competition was then dropped out of sensitivity following the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Tech_massacre" title="Virginia Tech massacre">Virginia Tech massacre</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fight_song">Fight song</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Fight song">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/The_Cavalier_Song" title="The Cavalier Song">The Cavalier Song</a> is the official fight song of the University of Virginia. The song was a result of a contest held in 1923 by the University. The Cavalier Song, with lyrics by Lawrence Haywood Lee, Jr. and music by <a href="/wiki/Fulton_Lewis" title="Fulton Lewis">Fulton Lewis, Jr.</a>, was selected as the winner.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> Generally the second half of the song is played during sporting events. Until the 2008 football season, the entire fight song could be heard during the <a href="/wiki/Cavalier_Marching_Band" title="Cavalier Marching Band">Cavalier Marching Band</a>'s entrance at home football games.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>Student life at the University of Virginia is marked by a number of unique traditions. The campus of the University is referred to as &quot;the Grounds.&quot; Freshmen, sophomores, juniors, and seniors are instead called first-, second-, third-, and fourth-years in order to reflect Jefferson's belief that learning is a never-ending process, rather than one to be completed within four years. Also, students do not &quot;graduate&quot; from the University; instead, they &quot;take&quot; their degrees. Professors are traditionally addressed as &quot;Mr.&quot; or &quot;Ms.&quot; instead of &quot;Doctor&quot; (although medical doctors are the exception and are called &quot;Doctor&quot;) in deference to Thomas Jefferson's desire to have an equality of ideas, discriminated by merit and unburdened by title.</p> 
     <p>In 2005, the University was named &quot;Hottest for Fitness&quot; by <i><a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a></i> magazine,<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> due in part to 94% of its students using one of the four indoor athletics facilities. Particularly popular is the Aquatics and Fitness Center, situated across the street from the Alderman Dorms.</p> 
     <p>The University of Virginia sent more workers to the <a href="/wiki/Peace_Corps" title="Peace Corps">Peace Corps</a> in 2006<sup id="cite_ref-Peace_Corps1_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peace_Corps1-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> and 2008<sup id="cite_ref-Peace_Corps2_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peace_Corps2-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> than any other &quot;medium-sized&quot; university in the United States. Volunteerism at the University is centered in Madison House which offers numerous opportunities to serve others. Among the numerous programs offered are tutoring, housing improvement, and an organization called Hoos Against Hunger, which gives leftover food from restaurants to the homeless of Charlottesville, rather than allowing it to be discarded.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Amphitheater_at_Univ._of_VA_IMG_4274.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Amphitheater_at_Univ._of_VA_IMG_4274.JPG/200px-Amphitheater_at_Univ._of_VA_IMG_4274.JPG" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Amphitheater_at_Univ._of_VA_IMG_4274.JPG/300px-Amphitheater_at_Univ._of_VA_IMG_4274.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Amphitheater_at_Univ._of_VA_IMG_4274.JPG/400px-Amphitheater_at_Univ._of_VA_IMG_4274.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Amphitheater_at_Univ._of_VA_IMG_4274.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The University Amphitheater
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>A number of <a href="/wiki/Secret_Societies_at_the_University_of_Virginia" title="Secret Societies at the University of Virginia" class="mw-redirect">secret societies at the University</a>, most notably the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Society" title="Seven Society">Seven Society</a>, <a href="/wiki/Z_Society" title="Z Society">Z Society</a>, and <a href="/wiki/IMP_Society" title="IMP Society">IMP Society</a>, have operated for decades, leaving their painted marks on University buildings. Other significant secret societies include <a href="/wiki/Eli_Banana" title="Eli Banana">Eli Banana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Secret_societies_at_the_University_of_Virginia#T.I.L.K.A." title="Secret societies at the University of Virginia">T.I.L.K.A.</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Secret_societies_at_the_University_of_Virginia#Purple_Shadows" title="Secret societies at the University of Virginia">Purple Shadows</a> (who commemorate Jefferson's birthday shortly after dawn on the Lawn each April 13), The Sons of Liberty, and the <a href="#Recent_societies">21 Society</a>. Not all the secret societies keep their membership unknown, but even those who don't hide their identities generally keep most of their good works and activities far from the public eye.</p> 
     <p>The student life building on the University of Virginia is called Newcomb Hall. It is home to the Student Activities Center (SAC) and the Media Activities Center (MAC), where student groups can get leadership consulting and use computing and copying resources, as well as several meeting rooms for student groups. Student Council, the student self-governing body, holds meetings Tuesdays at 6PM in the Newcomb South Meeting Room. Student Council, or &quot;StudCo,&quot; also holds office hours and regular committee meetings in the newly renovated Newcomb Programs and Council (PAC) Room. The PAC also houses the University Programs Council and Class Councils. Newcomb basement is home to both the office of the independent student newspaper <i>The Declaration</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Cavalier_Daily" title="The Cavalier Daily">The Cavalier Daily</a></i>, and the Consortium of University Publications.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Boyd_Tinsley_7-5-08_Rothbury_MI.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Boyd_Tinsley_7-5-08_Rothbury_MI.JPG/175px-Boyd_Tinsley_7-5-08_Rothbury_MI.JPG" width="175" height="299" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Boyd_Tinsley_7-5-08_Rothbury_MI.JPG/263px-Boyd_Tinsley_7-5-08_Rothbury_MI.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Boyd_Tinsley_7-5-08_Rothbury_MI.JPG/350px-Boyd_Tinsley_7-5-08_Rothbury_MI.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Boyd_Tinsley_7-5-08_Rothbury_MI.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Boyd_Tinsley" title="Boyd Tinsley">Boyd Tinsley</a>'s &quot;jam sessions&quot; would last for entire nights while he was a student at the University, attracting not only college musicians, but professional musicians as well; such as 
        <a href="/wiki/Jorma_Kaukonen" title="Jorma Kaukonen">Jorma Kaukonen</a> of 
        <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Airplane" title="Jefferson Airplane">Jefferson Airplane</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Student Societies have existed on grounds since the early 19th Century. The <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Literary_and_Debating_Society" title="Jefferson Literary and Debating Society">Jefferson Literary and Debating Society</a>, founded in 1825, is the second oldest Greek-Lettered organization in the nation (the oldest being the Phi Beta Kappa honor fraternity). It continues to meet every Friday at 7:29 PM in <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Hall" title="Jefferson Hall">Jefferson Hall</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Washington_Literary_Society_and_Debating_Union" title="Washington Literary Society and Debating Union">Washington Literary Society and Debating Union</a> also meets every week, and the two organizations often engage in a friendly rivalry. In the days before social fraternities existed and intercollegiate athletics became popular, these Societies were often the focal point of social activity on grounds.<sup id="cite_ref-Jefferson_Society_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jefferson_Society-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> Several fraternities were later founded at the University of Virginia including <a href="/wiki/Pi_Kappa_Alpha" title="Pi Kappa Alpha">Pi Kappa Alpha</a> (March 1, 1868) and <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Sigma" title="Kappa Sigma">Kappa Sigma</a> (December 10, 1869). Many of these fraternities are located on <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Road" title="Rugby Road">Rugby Road</a>.</p> 
     <p>A national publication's survey recently revealed that UVA's students give their library system higher marks than students at any other school in the United States. The best-known library is Alderman Library for the humanities and social sciences, which contains 10 floors of stacks with many useful study nooks hidden among them. UVA's renowned <a href="/wiki/Albert_and_Shirley_Small_Special_Collections_Library" title="Albert and Shirley Small Special Collections Library">Albert and Shirley Small Special Collections Library</a> features one of the premier collections of American Literature in the country as well as two copies of the <a href="/wiki/Dunlap_broadside" title="Dunlap broadside" class="mw-redirect">original printing</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence" title="United States Declaration of Independence">Declaration of Independence</a>. It was in this library in 2006 that Robert Stilling, an English Graduate Student, discovered an unpublished <a href="/wiki/Robert_Frost" title="Robert Frost">Robert Frost</a> poem from 1918.<sup id="cite_ref-Frost-Poem_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frost-Poem-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> Clemons Library, next to Alderman, is a popular study spot. Hundreds of students can be found gathered on its various quiet floors on any given night. Clark Hall, home of the Science &amp; Engineering Library, also scores high marks. One of the notable features of Clark Hall is the Mural Room, decorated by two three-panel murals by Allyn Cox, depicting the Moral Law and the Civil Law. The murals were finished and set in place in 1934.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> As of 2006<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=University_of_Virginia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the University and <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> were working on the digitization of selected collections from the library system.<sup id="cite_ref-Google_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Google-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>As at many universities, alcohol use is a part of the social life of many undergraduate students at the University. Concerns particularly arose about a past trend of fourth-year students consuming excessive alcohol during the day of the last home football game. This trend has been short lived, as the vast majority of undergraduates approach drinking in a responsible manner.,<sup id="cite_ref-4thYear5th_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4thYear5th-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> President Casteen announced a $2.5 million donation from <a href="/wiki/Anheuser-Busch" title="Anheuser-Busch">Anheuser-Busch</a> to fund a new UVA-based Social Norms Institute in September 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-SocialNorms_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SocialNorms-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> A spokesman said: &quot;the goal is to get students to emulate the positive behavior of the vast majority of students.&quot; However, based on ratings of sex, sports, and <a href="/wiki/Nightlife" title="Nightlife">nightlife</a>, the college was ranked at number one in <i><a href="/wiki/Playboy" title="Playboy">Playboy</a>'</i>s 2012 list of Top 10 Party Schools.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_safety">Student safety</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Student safety">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>While <a href="/wiki/Charlottesville" title="Charlottesville" class="mw-redirect">Charlottesville</a>, which typically registers zero to three murders per year, is generally considered a safe city, students have been involved on both sides of homicides in recent history.</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>On March 22, 1986, physiology graduate student Pat Collins disappeared after using an ATM in downtown Charlottesville. He was never found.</li> 
      <li>On November 8, 2003, student Andrew Alston stabbed an Albemarle County firefighter to death during a fight on 14th Street. His manslaughter sentence resulted in a jail term of three years, prompting allegations<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> of special treatment for students.</li> 
      <li>On May 3, 2010 in what has become known as the <a href="/wiki/Murder_of_Yeardley_Love" title="Murder of Yeardley Love">UVA Lacrosse Killing</a>, 22-year-old UVA <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_lacrosse" title="Women's lacrosse">women's lacrosse</a> player Yeardley Love was found unresponsive in her 14th Street apartment. Later that day, former romantic partner and then-current men's lacrosse player George Huguely was charged with her murder.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_events">Student events</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Student events">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>One of the largest events at the University of Virginia is called Springfest. It takes place every year in the spring, and features a large free concert and various inflatables and games.</p> 
     <p>Another popular event is <a href="/wiki/Foxfield_Races" title="Foxfield Races">Foxfield</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Steeplechase" title="Steeplechase">steeplechase</a> and social gathering that takes place nearby in <a href="/wiki/Albemarle_County" title="Albemarle County" class="mw-redirect">Albemarle County</a> in April, and which is annually attended by thousands of students from the University of Virginia and neighboring colleges.<sup id="cite_ref-foxfield_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foxfield-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honor_system">Honor system</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Honor system">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div style="float: right; margin: 0 0 0.5em 1em; width: 16.5em; text-align: right; font-size: 1em; font-family: verdana, lucida grande, sans-serif; line-height: normal;"> 
      <div style="border:1px solid #999; background:#fff; text-align:left; padding:1em; text-align:left;"> 
       <div align="center">
        <b>HONOR PLEDGE</b>
       </div> 
       <p>On my honor as a student, I have neither given nor received aid on this assignment/examination.</p> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Virginia has an honor code, formally known as the Honor System.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Honor_code" title="Honor code">Honor System</a> is usually student-run (though university administration interference has occurred, as described in the Leggett case below). It was founded by Virginia students in 1842 after John A. G. Davis, chairman of the faculty and professor of law, who was attempting to resolve a conflict between students, was shot to death.<sup id="cite_ref-dabney-honor_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dabney-honor-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> Originally, the student was expected to hold himself to a gentleman's code of conduct. In the wake of the shooting, law professor <a href="/wiki/Henry_St._George_Tucker,_Sr." title="Henry St. George Tucker, Sr.">Henry St. George Tucker, Sr.</a> proposed a basic honor pledge as a gesture of confidence in the honor of Virginia students.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> In modern times, however, the Honor System is composed of only three tenets: a student will not <a href="/wiki/Lie" title="Lie">lie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cheating" title="Cheating">cheat</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Theft" title="Theft">steal</a>. It extends to all matters academic and personal, and the sole sanction for a confirmed Honor System violation is dismissal from the University. This is called the &quot;single sanction&quot;.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Honorsystematuva.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Honorsystematuva.jpg/250px-Honorsystematuva.jpg" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Honorsystematuva.jpg/375px-Honorsystematuva.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Honorsystematuva.jpg/500px-Honorsystematuva.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Honorsystematuva.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> A plaque regarding 150 years of the Honor System, placed on the Lawn in 1992
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The system is not without its detractors ? it has been criticized because the required severe penalty may prevent more moderate violations from being reported or acted upon.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> As the system is entirely student run, a change to the Honor Committee constitution could have the effect of ending the single sanction system of punishment. Although students have voted on numerous proposals to weaken or eliminate the single sanction over the past few decades, none has ever succeeded. Support for the honor system has waned in recent years, and in the Spring of 2007 a non-binding referendum to replace the single sanction with a tiered, multiple sanction system received 49.5% of the votes cast, falling just 62 votes shy of a majority.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In theory, the Honor System allows the faculty to do such things as assign timed take-home examinations, and research or studies to be done in a particular way, with the assurance that the strictures placed on the student will be observed. However, no professor is required to extend such courtesies. The student is often required to sign all examinations or assignments with the following pledge: &quot;On my honor as a student, I have neither given nor received aid on this assignment/examination.&quot; The Honor System allows the student to purchase books and supplies on-Grounds upon giving his or her word to pay, and some members of the Charlottesville community accept the word of the student regarding off-Grounds business transactions.</p> 
     <p>While cheating convictions are relatively rare (24 students were dismissed during the 2003 academic year, and 21 more were dismissed in 2004), one large cheating scandal occurred in 2001. Physics professor and Hereford College Dean Louis Bloomfield, based on a student's complaint, had suspicions that some of his students had copied portions of their term papers from <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities" title="Fraternities and sororities" class="mw-redirect">fraternity</a> archives in his Introduction to Physics class. After devising a computer program to detect copied phrases of at least six sequential words, over 150 students were accused of plagiarizing or allowing others to plagiarize their work over the previous five semesters. Although over 100 of these students were eventually exonerated, 48 students either admitted guilt or were convicted, and were therefore dismissed from the University. Three of these students had already graduated, and their degrees were subsequently revoked.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <p>Lawsuits or threats of lawsuits have resulted in university administration pressure or outright interference in Honor system enforcement. The most notable instance was the 1993 case of Christopher Leggett, a student convicted of cheating.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> The Honor Committee insisted Leggett had received a fair trial but President <a href="/wiki/John_T._Casteen_III" title="John T. Casteen III">John Casteen</a> called it flawed, after Leggett's wealthy family hired the major Washington DC law firm <a href="/wiki/Williams_%26_Connolly" title="Williams &amp; Connolly">Williams &amp; Connolly</a> to threaten a lawsuit.<sup id="cite_ref-Wash_Post_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wash_Post-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup> Casteen directed a new Honor trial with special procedures dictated by Leggett's lawyers tailored just for his case, which resulted in an acquittal. At least one Honor Committee member resigned because of the administration interference.<sup id="cite_ref-Redinger_case_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Redinger_case-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_alumni">Notable alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Notable alumni">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Virginia_people" title="List of University of Virginia people">List of University of Virginia people</a>
